## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where dv/dt depends on velocity v and time t. The system likely involves nonlinear restoring forces, velocity-dependent damping, and/or periodic driving forces, with position potentially eliminated or encoded through time dependence.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (velocity-proportional friction)
- Quadratic velocity dependence: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 (nonlinear drag)
- Cubic velocity nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type oscillator)
- Van der Pol-type: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (self-excited oscillator with driving)
- Harmonic restoring via time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) (sinusoidal position-dependent restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (damped driven harmonic oscillator)
- Nonlinear restoring + damping: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c1 * t)**3 + c3 * v (Duffing-type with damping)
- Rayleigh dissipation: dv_dt = c0 * v * (1 + c1 * v**2) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (velocity-dependent damping with restoring)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v (parametrically excited oscillator)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c3 * t)**3 (full nonlinear oscillator)
- Polynomial velocity: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v + c2 * v**2 + c3 * v**3 (general polynomial phase-space model)
- Product coupling: dv_dt = c0 * v * sin(c1 * t) (multiplicative velocity-time coupling)
- Limit cycle form: dv_dt = c0 * v * (c1 - v**2) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (amplitude-limiting dynamics with drive)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Periodic driving force → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms in the acceleration equation
- Self-sustained oscillation / limit cycles → velocity terms of the form v*(1 - c*v²) indicating amplitude stabilization
- Nonlinear restoring force expressed via time → sin³(c*t) or polynomial powers of sin(c*t) when position is sinusoidal
- Parametric excitation → products of v with periodic functions of t, e.g., v*cos(c*t)
- Odd-symmetry nonlinearity in velocity → only odd powers of v (v, v³, v⁵) preserving time-reversal symmetry of oscillation
- Phase-space closure → if dv/dt depends only on v (no explicit t), the system is autonomous with conserved quantities
- Frequency mixing in driven nonlinear systems → multiple sinusoidal terms with different frequencies or harmonics
- Energy injection/dissipation balance → competing positive and negative v-dependent terms leading to stable amplitude

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `0.106256914230442*sin(t) - 0.484396978017638*sin(v) - 0.968793956035275*v`

The GT has three terms:
1. A constant times `sin(t)`
2. A constant times `sin(v)`
3. A constant times `v`

Note that `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2)`, so `c1*cos(c2 + t)` with `c2 = -π/2` gives `c1*sin(t)`. This handles the sin(t) term.

The key challenge is the `sin(v)` term. Most candidates have `c0*v + c1*cos(c2 + t)` plus additional terms. I need to find one that can produce `-0.484396978017638*sin(v)`.

Let me check candidates that contain `sin(c*v + ...)`:

**Candidate 4**: `c0*v + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*sin(c4*v + c5)`
Setting c4=1, c5=0: `c0*v + c1*cos(c2+t) + c3*sin(v)`. With c2=-π/2, c1=0.106..., c3=-0.484..., c0=-0.968... This gives exactly the GT! ✓

**Candidate 27**: `c0*v + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*sin(c4 + c5*v) + c6*v`
Same idea, setting c5=1, c4=0: works too.

**Candidate 24**: `c0*v + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*sin(c4*t + c5*v + c6)`
Setting c4=0, c5=1, c6=0: `c0*v + c1*cos(c2+t) + c3*sin(v)`. Works! ✓

**Candidate 1**: `c0*v + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*sin(c4*v + c5) + c6*v*cos(c7*t + c8) + c9*v`
Setting c4=1, c5=0, c6=0: reduces to `(c0+c9)*v + c1*cos(c2+t) + c3*sin(v)`. Works! ✓

**Candidate 42**: `c0*v + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*sin(c4*v + c5) + c6*v**3`
Setting c6=0, c4=1, c5=0: works! ✓

**Candidate 73**: `c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*sin(c4*v + c5) + c6*v + c7 + (c8 + v)**3`
Expanding (c8+v)³ = c8³ + 3c8²v + 3c8v² + v³. To eliminate v³ and v² terms, we need the v³ coefficient = 1 (always), so this can't work since we can't eliminate v³.

Let me verify **Candidate 4** carefully:
- GT: `0.106256914230442*sin(t) - 0.484396978017638*sin(v) - 0.968793956035275*v`

- Set c3 = -0.484396978017638, c4 = 1, c5 = 0
